class \mbox{\hyperlink{classph_1_1math_1_1_t_heaviside_step2_d}{THeaviside\+Step2D}}
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em A step function in 2-\/D, with a specific normal direction. This is a simplified version of general Heaviside step function in 2-\/D. This class represents 1-\/D Heaviside in 2-\/D, dividing the xy-\/plane into regions of value 0 \& 1 (while a general Heaviside step function in 2-\/D can have the discontinuity along an arbitarary 2-\/D contour, this class {\itshape does not} support that). Value along the line of discontinuity is 0.\+5 (for integer types, this would be 0). \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

concept \mbox{\hyperlink{conceptph_1_1math_1_1_c_supports_spectral_conversions}{CSupports\+Spectral\+Conversions}}
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Basic requirements a spectral color space definition must satisfy in addition to CHas\+Color\+Space\+Properties. Bound tristimulus color space\+: A spectral color space must choose a tristimulus color space as its binding space, which will be used by color space operations that cannot operate in the spectral space. The chosen color space is often referred to as "{}bound space"{} for simplicity. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Generate 32-\/bit hash values using Murmur\+Hash3. Note that there are no collisions when {\ttfamily T} has \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}= 32 bits (two distinct inputs will not result in the same output). In general, if there is a way to reverse a function (reversing {\ttfamily \doxylink{namespaceph_1_1math_a45d86025b912ecd026e05d1aa6130d2c}{murmur3\+\_\+32()}} is possible), it is guaranteed there cannot be any collisions. \Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_ab6c812780186db6fffc4e5b25946f17e}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_ab6c812780186db6fffc4e5b25946f17e} 
\index{ph::math@{ph::math}!black\_body\_spectral\_radiance\_at@{black\_body\_spectral\_radiance\_at}}
\index{black\_body\_spectral\_radiance\_at@{black\_body\_spectral\_radiance\_at}!ph::math@{ph::math}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{black\_body\_spectral\_radiance\_at()}{black\_body\_spectral\_radiance\_at()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T $>$ \\
T ph\+::math\+::black\+\_\+body\+\_\+spectral\+\_\+radiance\+\_\+at (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const T}]{temperatureK,  }\item[{const T}]{wavelength\+NM }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Get Black-\/body spectral radiance at specific temperature and wavelength. Note that this function is not returning radiance but spectral radiance. The returned spectral radiance has the unit of watt per steradian per square meter per meter (W \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} sr\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} m\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} m\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/1). 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em temperatureK} & Temperature in Kelvin. \\
\hline
{\em wavelength\+NM} & Wavelength of the interest, in nanometers. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Emitted spectral radiance on specified parameters, in SI unit (W \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} sr\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} m\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} m\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/1). 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_a2e1994639e2978dc226efa4ef08cbec5}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_a2e1994639e2978dc226efa4ef08cbec5}

\index{black\_body\_spectral\_radiance\_curve@{black\_body\_spectral\_radiance\_curve}!ph::math@{ph::math}}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T $>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ T $>$ ph\+::math\+::black\+\_\+body\+\_\+spectral\+\_\+radiance\+\_\+curve (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const T}]{temperatureK,  }\item[{const T}]{lambda\+Min\+NM,  }\item[{const T}]{lambda\+Max\+NM,  }\item[{const std\+::size\+\_\+t}]{num\+Curve\+Points,  }\item[{std\+::vector$<$ T $>$ \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}const}]{out\+\_\+lambda\+Values = {\ttfamily nullptr} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Get a curve for Black-\/body radiation. Note that this function is not returning radiance but spectral radiance. The returned spectral radiance has the unit of watt per steradian per square meter per meter (W \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} sr\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} m\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} m\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/1). 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em lambda\+Min\+NM} & Minimum wavelength of the curve data, in nanometers. \\
\hline
{\em lambda\+Max\+NM} & Maximum wavelength of the curve data, in nanometers. \\
\hline
{\em num\+Curve\+Points} & Number of points for the curve. Evenly spaced in \mbox{[}lambda\+Min\+NM, lambda\+Max\+NM\mbox{]}. Must be \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}= 2. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Emitted spectral radiance on each wavelength, in SI unit (W \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} sr\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} m\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} m\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/1). 
\end{DoxyReturn}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , std\+::enable\+\_\+if\+\_\+t$<$!std\+::is\+\_\+floating\+\_\+point\+\_\+v$<$ T $>$, int $>$  = 0$>$ \\
T ph\+::math\+::clamp (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const T}]{value,  }\item[{const T}]{lower\+Bound,  }\item[{const T}]{upper\+Bound }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Clamps a integer value in \mbox{[}lower\+Bound, upper\+Bound\mbox{]}. 

Clamps a float value in \mbox{[}lower\+Bound, upper\+Bound\mbox{]}. If a floating-\/point value is NaN, its value is clamped to lower bound. Neither lower bound or upper bound can be NaN, or the method\textquotesingle{}s behavior is undefined. \Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_af11f191a13f32e5ff37ba539bb731029}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_af11f191a13f32e5ff37ba539bb731029}

std\+::size\+\_\+t ph\+::math\+::discrete\+\_\+spatial\+\_\+hash (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Integer}]{x,  }\item[{Integer}]{y,  }\item[{Integer}]{z,  }\item[{std\+::size\+\_\+t}]{hash\+Table\+Size }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

Implements the hash function described in the paper "{}\+Optimized Spatial  \+Hashing for Collision Detection of Deformable Objects"{}. Note that although they stated in the paper that 73856093, 19349663 and 83492791 are all prime numbers, 19349663 is in fact a composite number (41 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} 471943).

Reference\+: \href{http://www.beosil.com/download/CollisionDetectionHashing_VMV03.pdf}{\texttt{ http\+://www.\+beosil.\+com/download/\+Collision\+Detection\+Hashing\+\_\+\+VMV03.\+pdf}} \Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_a2c27c006cdd87270cab6bb88e7036136}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_a2c27c006cdd87270cab6bb88e7036136}

\index{ph::math@{ph::math}!fast\_rcp\_sqrt@{fast\_rcp\_sqrt}}
\index{fast\_rcp\_sqrt@{fast\_rcp\_sqrt}!ph::math@{ph::math}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{fast\_rcp\_sqrt()}{fast\_rcp\_sqrt()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily float ph\+::math\+::fast\+\_\+rcp\+\_\+sqrt (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{float}]{x }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Computes {\ttfamily 1/sqrt(x)} in a fast but approximative way. 

This method is best known for its implementation in Quake III Arena (1999). Here the implementation follows what described in the referenced paper, which uses a slightly better (in terms of maximal relative error) magic number.

Reference\+: \href{http://www.lomont.org/Math/Papers/2003/InvSqrt.pdf}{\texttt{ http\+://www.\+lomont.\+org/\+Math/\+Papers/2003/\+Inv\+Sqrt.\+pdf}} \Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_adb93254f78909d9fef4bc8d7326b7670}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_adb93254f78909d9fef4bc8d7326b7670}

\Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_a91780ac8e52ddfdd3f0314cc36b882c2}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_a91780ac8e52ddfdd3f0314cc36b882c2} 
\index{ph::math@{ph::math}!fp32\_to\_fp16\_bits@{fp32\_to\_fp16\_bits}}
\index{fp32\_to\_fp16\_bits@{fp32\_to\_fp16\_bits}!ph::math@{ph::math}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{fp32\_to\_fp16\_bits()}{fp32\_to\_fp16\_bits()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint16 ph\+::math\+::fp32\+\_\+to\+\_\+fp16\+\_\+bits (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const float32}]{value }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Convert a 32-\/bit float to 16-\/bit representation. 

The implementation of half floats does not contain "{}safety checks"{}, i.\+e., according to IEEE 754-\/2008, +/-\/65504 is the max representable value of half floats, input values that exceed the max value will not be represented correctly and will cause problems in Open\+GL or other APIs. If the input (fp32) is too samll, 0 will be returned. \Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_a9460c87b6dab3097ee4d084d9b59a604}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_a9460c87b6dab3097ee4d084d9b59a604}

T ph\+::math\+::fractional\+\_\+part (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const T}]{value }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Retrieve the fractional part of {\ttfamily value} (with the sign unchanged). The result is not guaranteed to be the same as the bit representation of 

\textquotesingle{}s fractional part. The result is undefined if input value is NaN or +-\/Inf.

A Murmur\+Hash3-\/style bit mixer that outperforms the original by quite some margin. 64-\/bit version. 

\Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_a45d86025b912ecd026e05d1aa6130d2c}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_a45d86025b912ecd026e05d1aa6130d2c} 
\index{ph::math@{ph::math}!murmur3\_32@{murmur3\_32}}
\index{murmur3\_32@{murmur3\_32}!ph::math@{ph::math}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{murmur3\_32()}{murmur3\_32()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T $>$ \\
uint32 ph\+::math\+::murmur3\+\_\+32 (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const T \&}]{data,  }\item[{uint32}]{seed }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Generate 32-\/bit hash values using Murmur\+Hash3. Note that there are no collisions when {\ttfamily T} has \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}= 32 bits (two distinct inputs will not result in the same output). In general, if there is a way to reverse a function (reversing {\ttfamily \doxylink{namespaceph_1_1math_a45d86025b912ecd026e05d1aa6130d2c}{murmur3\+\_\+32()}} is possible), it is guaranteed there cannot be any collisions. Otherwise, it would not be possible to revert.

\Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_a4690860b243fe5e072ff6048732ae2a3}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_a4690860b243fe5e072ff6048732ae2a3} 
\index{ph::math@{ph::math}!normalize\_integer@{normalize\_integer}}
\index{normalize\_integer@{normalize\_integer}!ph::math@{ph::math}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{normalize\_integer()}{normalize\_integer()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$std\+::floating\+\_\+point Float\+Type, std\+::integral Int\+Type$>$ \\
Float\+Type ph\+::math\+::normalize\+\_\+integer (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Int\+Type}]{int\+Val }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



\doxylink{classph_1_1math_1_1_transform}{Transform} an integer to the range \mbox{[}0, 1\mbox{]} (\mbox{[}-\/1, 1\mbox{]} for signed integer). When transforming an unsigned integer, the minimum value the integer can hold will be mapped to 0, while the maximum value will be mapped to 1; the rest of the integer values will be uniformally mapped to the range \mbox{[}0, 1\mbox{]}. Signed integer types follow the same rule, except the mapped range will be \mbox{[}-\/1, 1\mbox{]}. 

\Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_a413c0ea914fc11e1f26bfabd44d2c162}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_a413c0ea914fc11e1f26bfabd44d2c162}

\index{normalize\_samples\_energy@{normalize\_samples\_energy}!ph::math@{ph::math}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{normalize\_samples\_energy()}{normalize\_samples\_energy()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , CSpectral\+Sample\+Props Sample\+Props = Default\+Spectral\+Sample\+Props$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceph_1_1math_ab6e489b4814390fb4f1a68257d8d432d}{TSpectral\+Sample\+Values}}$<$ T, Sample\+Props $>$ ph\+::math\+::normalize\+\_\+samples\+\_\+energy (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceph_1_1math_ab6e489b4814390fb4f1a68257d8d432d}{TSpectral\+Sample\+Values}}$<$ T, Sample\+Props $>$ \&}]{src\+Samples }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Normalize spectral samples as if they carry energy. Normalized spectral samples, together, represents the expected amount of energy that 1 unit of total energy would distribute on each wavelength interval (implying that the samples should sum to 1). 

\Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_a97853fb83b95a1bd4eb7c30cfce31938}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_a97853fb83b95a1bd4eb7c30cfce31938}

Same as {\ttfamily \doxylink{namespaceph_1_1math_a127b033f884f9a76ea631ddf02fc1d0f}{radical\+\_\+inverse()}}, with permutation ability. It is guaranteed that no more than {\ttfamily \doxylink{namespaceph_1_1math_1_1radical__inverse__detail_a3b137ffa4261d6ac227aee60ba61dd7c}{radical\+\_\+inverse\+\_\+detail\+::num\+\_\+meaningful\+\_\+digits()}} digits will be processed during the radical inverse.

\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\index{ph::math@{ph::math}!relative\_luminance@{relative\_luminance}}
\index{relative\_luminance@{relative\_luminance}!ph::math@{ph::math}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{relative\_luminance()}{relative\_luminance()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceph_1_1math_a957eab3ceed525ebce5c24b6b57eb975}{EColor\+Space}} SRC\+\_\+\+COLOR\+\_\+\+SPACE, typename T , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceph_1_1math_aeb6d400f8c4f85be266ab51b3cd65951}{EChromatic\+Adaptation}} ALGORITHM = EChromatic\+Adaptation\+::\+Default$>$ \\
T ph\+::math\+::relative\+\_\+luminance (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const auto \&}]{src\+Color\+Values,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceph_1_1math_a821af6da20aaed56cc09ad440633d067}{EColor\+Usage}}}]{usage = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceph_1_1math_a821af6da20aaed56cc09ad440633d067a8d4c0b2cef256d21ab680366c8b1c6bf}{EColor\+Usage\+::\+EMR}}} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Relative luminance of {\ttfamily src\+Color\+Values}. Normally for a tristimulus color, its reference white\textquotesingle{}s relative luminance will be 1. For spectral samples, it is the result of performing an inner product with the luminous efficiency function. For ECF usages, its relative luminance is guaranteed to be within \mbox{[}0, 1\mbox{]}. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\index{ph::math@{ph::math}!resample\_black\_body\_spectral\_radiance@{resample\_black\_body\_spectral\_radiance}}
\index{resample\_black\_body\_spectral\_radiance@{resample\_black\_body\_spectral\_radiance}!ph::math@{ph::math}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{resample\_black\_body\_spectral\_radiance()}{resample\_black\_body\_spectral\_radiance()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , CSpectral\+Sample\+Props Sample\+Props = Default\+Spectral\+Sample\+Props$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceph_1_1math_ab6e489b4814390fb4f1a68257d8d432d}{TSpectral\+Sample\+Values}}$<$ T, Sample\+Props $>$ ph\+::math\+::resample\+\_\+black\+\_\+body\+\_\+spectral\+\_\+radiance (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{T}]{temperatureK }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



SPD of black-\/body radiation in spectral radiance. Note that this function is not returning radiance but spectral radiance. The returned spectral radiance has the unit of watt per steradian per square meter per meter (W \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} sr\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/1 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} m\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/2 \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} m\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}-\/1). If radiance is desired, use {\ttfamily \doxylink{namespaceph_1_1math_a9f6174bc51d3f6c8d98447fa0150d0a4}{resample\+\_\+black\+\_\+body\+\_\+radiance()}}. If a normalized energy distribution is desired, use {\ttfamily \doxylink{namespaceph_1_1math_affd528849118d3a6a18bc509629ea485}{resample\+\_\+black\+\_\+body()}}. 

\Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_ac3d128c7225063c77e89c60595769355}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_ac3d128c7225063c77e89c60595769355}

\Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_a3b208c3dfc7024c379877d689ae7db08}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_a3b208c3dfc7024c379877d689ae7db08} 
\index{ph::math@{ph::math}!resample\_illuminant\_E@{resample\_illuminant\_E}}
\index{resample\_illuminant\_E@{resample\_illuminant\_E}!ph::math@{ph::math}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{resample\_illuminant\_E()}{resample\_illuminant\_E()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , CSpectral\+Sample\+Props Sample\+Props = Default\+Spectral\+Sample\+Props$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceph_1_1math_ab6e489b4814390fb4f1a68257d8d432d}{TSpectral\+Sample\+Values}}$<$ T, Sample\+Props $>$ ph\+::math\+::resample\+\_\+illuminant\+\_\+E (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



SPD of standard illuminants. Any light source which statistically has the same relative SPD as a standard illuminant can be considered a standard light source, and is the reason why the SPD resample functions return a energy-\/normalized SPD (for convenience, as this is what you want almost always). 

SPD of standard illuminants E, with total energy = 1. \Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_a8ae6d9df536ec07a0411c503df56fee6}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_a8ae6d9df536ec07a0411c503df56fee6}

\Hypertarget{namespaceph_1_1math_a7377d0dddd537e4e7a04f98bd8e1114e}\label{namespaceph_1_1math_a7377d0dddd537e4e7a04f98bd8e1114e} 
\index{ph::math@{ph::math}!sign@{sign}}
\index{sign@{sign}!ph::math@{ph::math}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{sign()}{sign()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T $>$ \\
int ph\+::math\+::sign (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const T}]{value }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Extract the sign of {\ttfamily value}. 

Function is defined only if the provided value is comparable to 0. Note that the input is passed by value.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
1 when {\ttfamily value} \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 0; -\/1 when {\ttfamily value} \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} 0; 0 when {\ttfamily value} == 0. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This function is branchless. 
\end{DoxyNote}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{wrap()}{wrap()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , std\+::enable\+\_\+if\+\_\+t$<$ std\+::is\+\_\+integral\+\_\+v$<$ T $>$, int $>$  = 0$>$ \\
T ph\+::math\+::wrap (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{T}]{value,  }\item[{const T}]{lower\+Bound,  }\item[{const T}]{upper\+Bound }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Wraps an integer around \mbox{[}lower-\/bound, upper-\/bound\mbox{]}. For example, given a bound \mbox{[}-\/1, 2\mbox{]}, 3 will be wrapped to -\/1.
